                           <mi mathvariant="normal">a</mi>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}{\mathrm {log}}\,i = {\mathrm b}\,{\mathrm {log}}\,v + {\mathrm {log}}\,{\mathrm a}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(2)</span></div>
         </div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202305190-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f1e7ef48-c975-4f77-aef8-566c49f83400/adma202305190-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f1e7ef48-c975-4f77-aef8-566c49f83400/adma202305190-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/1c2be3fc-ff6a-4fe8-af09-09a7300af72f/adma202305190-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f1e7ef48-c975-4f77-aef8-566c49f83400/adma202305190-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202305190-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202305190" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves of the CoPS@C@N-CNF electrode at various scan rates. b) The calculated b values at four redox peaks for the CoPS@C@N-CNF electrode. c) CV curve of the CoPS@C@N-CNF electrode with the surface capacitive contribution at 2.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>. d) The percentage of capacitive contribution of the three electrodes at diverse scan rates. e) GITT curves of the three electrodes and their D<sub>Na+</sub> values f) for the initial cycle. Schematic (g), GCD profiles at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (h), cycling stability at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (i), and rate capability at different rates (j) of the CoPS@C@N-CNF//NVP@C full cell, of which yellow ball represents the Na<sup>+</sup> ion in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5g</a>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Note that <i>b</i> value is a very crucial power-law variable in the above formulas since the magnitude of its value directly reflects the kinetics contribution of the electrode after taking the logarithm. The calculated b values for the CoPS@C@N-CNF (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5b</a>), which are linearly fitted by taking the marked reduction and oxidation peaks in CV curves, are ≈0.86, 0.91, 0.97, and 0.92 at peaks A, B, C, and D, respectively, illustrating that the electrochemical charge-storage of the CoPS@C@N-CNF is influenced by the fast surface-capacitive behaviors, thereby inducing an outstanding rate character. Under the circumstances, we further employ the CV plots of diverse scan rates to accurately ascertain the contributions caused by the Na<sup>+</sup>-diffusion or the double-layer capacitance by using the relevant relationship of <i>i</i>&nbsp;=&nbsp;k<sub>1</sub>&nbsp;<i>v</i>&nbsp;+&nbsp;k<sub>2</sub> <i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> for the detailed calculation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202305190-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202305190-bib-0016_R_d17071639e1717" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Chem. Eng. J.">16</a>, <a href="#adma202305190-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202305190-bib-0043_R_d17071639e1717" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - J. Mater. Chem. A">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Among them, k<sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and k<sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> signify the non-faraday and faraday reactions, respectively. Therefore, the total contribution ratios of capacitor-like current at each certain scan rate were estimated. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5c</a> together with Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18c</a> (Supporting Information), f sketch intuitively the integral area of the capacitor-like current (marked as yellow-green area) in CV curve with that of the overall current achieved at 2.0&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, it is 89.2% for CoPS@C@N-CNF, 88.2% for CoS@C@N-CNF, and 86.5% for CoP<sub>2</sub>@C@N-CNF, meaning the surface capacitive behaviors of the three electrodes are dominating at this scan rate. Likewise, the percentages of the surface-capacitive contribution of the three electrodes at each scan rate were also calculated and summarized in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5d</a>. It manifests that, in contrast to two reference electrodes, the CoPS@C@N-CNF possesses better capacitive-contribution ratios at all scan rates, which illustrates again that ternary metal phosphosulfide has a prominent contribution in improving capacitive characteristics.</p>
         
         <p>The distinct difference in Na<sup>+</sup>-diffusion kinetics between three electrodes during the sodiation–desodition processes was initially explored by galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) tests based on simplified Fick's second law and related Equation,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202305190-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202305190-bib-0043_R_d17071639e1749" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - J. Mater. Chem. A">43</a>, <a href="#adma202305190-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202305190-bib-0063_R_d17071639e1749" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Small Methods">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which can be explicitly elaborated in the Supporting Information. Meanwhile, the test condition of GITT involves a sequence of constant currents (0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) with a pulsed time of 600&nbsp;s and a relaxation time of 3600&nbsp;s throughout the overall region of related voltage. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5e</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a> (Supporting Information) are the representative initial GITT profiles of three electrodes and an illustration view of the Na<sup>+</sup>-diffusion coefficient (D<sub>Na+</sub>) obtained by a locally enlarged current pulse of the CoPS@C@N-CNF electrode, respectively. Through calculation (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5g</a>), the D<sub>Na+</sub> values of the three electrodes for the initial cycle manifest similar evolution tendency and the range of D<sub>Na+</sub> values fluctuates between 10<sup>−8</sup> and 10<sup>−11</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> during the sodation–desodiation. Even so, the CoPS@C@N-CNF has relatively highest D<sub>Na+</sub> values in both sodiation and desodiation processes amongst three electrodes, which are next to the CoS@C@N-CNF and CoP<sub>2</sub>@C@N-CNF, matching well with the mentioned-above capacitive contribution testing. In addition, the decrease of the D<sub>Na+</sub> values during Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation maybe caused by the influx of vast Na<sup>+</sup> ions, inducing the structural evolution.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202305190-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202305190-bib-0027_R_d17071639e1794" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Chem. Eng. J.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to the above kinetics analysis and GITT results, it forcefully verifies that the CoPS@C@N-CNF possesses more outstanding surface capacitive features and Na<sup>+</sup>-diffusion capability than the other two, which makes for its significant ion-migration ability, fast reaction kinetics, and excellent rate properties.</p>
         
         <p>Taking into consideration of fast transportation ability and durable structural characteristics, the CoPS@C@N-CNF was employed as an anode host to set up an SIB full cell. As manifested in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5g</a>, the SIBs full cell is manufactured involving the CoPS@C@N-CNF anode, commercial-level Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C (NVP@C) cathode (denoted as CoPS@C@N-CNF//NVP@C) and glass fiber separator to explore the capability of practical applications. Notably, the NVP@C was purchased from Guangdong Canrd New Energy Technology Co., Ltd. Meanwhile, the related characterizations of the NVP@C on electrochemical performance and crystalline phase are afforded in Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20,S21</a> (Supporting Information). One can see from GCD profiles of full cells that it can afford the attractive discharge and charge capacities of ≈379.1 and 1196.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, contributing to an ICE of ≈31.7% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5h</a>). Going through 300 continuous loops (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5i</a>), the full cell still contributes a considerable capacity reaching ≈153.0&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Even after suffering a very long cycle of 1000 loops at a high rate of 3.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22</a>, Supporting Information), the CoPS@C@N-CNF//NVP@C full cell still obtains a discharge capacity of ≈84.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Subsequently, we performed the rate capability of the CoPS@C@N-CNF//NVP@C full cell at diverse rates. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0005">5j</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a> (Supporting Information), the full cell realizes the satisfactory rate performance, harvesting the average reversible capacities of 294.1, 265.1, 240.1, 224.5, 211.4, and 198.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at the rates of 0.2 to 3.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Surprisingly, the average capacities at a rate range of 1.0 to 3.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> are close to each other, suggesting the remarkable rate capability of full cells. Afterward, the specific capacity rapidly restored to 255.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> setting back to the initial rate of 0.2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, affording a great proof-of-feasibility in new-style energy storage devices.</p>
         
         <p>More performance enhancement understanding on possible adsorption energy of Na<sup>+</sup> ion, charge difference features, and Na<sup>+</sup>-migration energy barrier for three samples was further implemented via density functional theory (DFT) calculations. Given the circumstances of N-CNF and MOFs-derived carbon existing in the three materials mentioned above, meanwhile, they only perform to improve the charge transfer, induce interface resistance, and enhance the mechanical endurance of the electrode. Hence, the construction of the simplified CoPS, CoS, and CoP<sub>2</sub> models is fully capable of analyzing the reason for performance enhancement. First, the CoPS, CoS, and CoP<sub>2</sub> models after geometry optimization in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> (Supporting Information) show that the blue, yellow, and brown, balls respectively stand for the Co, S, and P atoms. Afterward, we further explored thoroughly the adsorption ability of three models for Na<sup>+</sup> ion, and the optimized adsorption structural configurations with the adsorption of four Na atoms on these three models are depicted in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0006">6a</a>. Calculations manifest that the Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption energy (Δ<i>E</i><sub>ads</sub>) of the CoPS model reaches −5.83&nbsp;eV, obviously lower than that of the CoS (−4.51&nbsp;eV) and CoP<sub>2</sub> (−4.33&nbsp;eV), symbolizing that Na atom is more handily adsorbed on ternary CoPS model than the other two. Meanwhile, the Δ<i>E</i><sub>ads</sub> of three models with different numbers of Na atoms were performed, as summarized in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information). Obviously, the CoPS model obtains the Δ<i>E</i><sub>ads</sub> of ≈−1.47, −2.48, −4.81, and −5.83&nbsp;eV as one, two, three, and four sodium atoms were respectively adsorbed on the CoPS model, which also exceeds those of the CoS and CoP<sub>2</sub> models, further confirming best Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption ability of the CoPS in three models. Additionally, the Δ<i>E</i><sub>ads</sub> of three models with the adsorption of one Na atom at different adsorption sites were also explored (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a>, Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information), Obviously, the different adsorption sites for Na atom in three models have a slight effect on the Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption energy, particularly, the CoPS model still offers best Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption energy at all four adsorption sites as comparison to the other two models.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202305190-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/58b13ff8-cb93-41f5-94c5-9a3bf8a10500/adma202305190-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/58b13ff8-cb93-41f5-94c5-9a3bf8a10500/adma202305190-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/9d773e53-265b-474d-91a9-a0ce6248af84/adma202305190-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/58b13ff8-cb93-41f5-94c5-9a3bf8a10500/adma202305190-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202305190-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202305190" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Optimized structural configurations for the four Na atoms adsorption on the simplified CoPS, CoS, and CoP<sub>2</sub> models; b) the corresponding charge density difference maps of three models. c) Na migration paths and d) corresponding energy barriers in CoPS, CoS, and CoP<sub>2</sub> models, in which the blue, brown, yellow, and brownish-yellow balls denote Co, P, S, and Na atoms, respectively. e) Diagrammatic drawing of significant electrochemical Na<sup>+</sup>-storage of hierarchical branch-leaf-shaped CoPS@C@N-CNF, in which the blue, pink, and yellow, brown balls denote Co, P, S atoms, respectively, while the rufous ball represents Na<sup>+</sup> ion.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The differential charge density analysis of the CoPS, CoS, and CoP<sub>2</sub> models with the adsorption of four Na atoms (denoted as CoPS-Na, CoS-Na, and CoP<sub>2</sub>-Na) was conducted to understand the trend of electron transfer. As illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0006">6b</a>, the remarkable color regions marked by cyan and yellow stand for electron depletion and gain, respectively. Distinctly, the charge difference contour plots manifest the significant transfer of the valence electrons, wherein the Na atoms deplete electrons while the surface of CoPS, CoS, and CoP<sub>2</sub> models accumulates electrons, revealing their good capturing ability for Na<sup>+</sup> ions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202305190-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202305190-bib-0005_R_d17071639e1961" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the amount of electron transfer was computed with the aid of the Bader charge analysis. Through analysis, the number of Bader charges shifted from the four Na adatoms to CoPS is ≈3.34 e<sup>−</sup>, superior to that of CoS-Na (3.25 e<sup>−</sup>) and CoP<sub>2</sub>-Na (3.02 e<sup>−</sup>). The stronger charge transfer of the CoPS model means a more significant Na<sup>+</sup>-ion adsorption, which is in agreement with the ΔE<sub>ads</sub> conclusion.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202305190-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202305190-bib-0064_R_d17071639e1979" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - J. Energy Chem.">64</a>, <a href="#adma202305190-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202305190-bib-0065_R_d17071639e1979" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> More importantly, after adsorbing different amounts of Na atoms on these three models, the amount of charge transfer from Na atoms follows the changing trend of adsorption energy (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information). In addition, we calculated the Na<sup>+</sup>-migration energy barriers of three models to further distinguish their kinetics properties, the structural models and the corresponding results are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0006">6c,d</a>. Obviously, Na can diffuse on the surface of the CoPS model with a diffusion energy barrier (0.22&nbsp;eV), much lower than that of the CoS (0.36&nbsp;eV) and CoP<sub>2</sub> (0.40&nbsp;eV) models. The lowest energy barrier of the CoPS model for Na<sup>+</sup>-migration is in accordance with the experimental best rate capability.</p>
         
         <p>In brief, this promotion analysis depending on theoretical computational results and experimental data-supporting sufficiently demonstrates that the significant electrochemical capability of the CoPS@C@N-CNF is mainly associated with its hierarchical branch-leaf architecture with unique multi-dimensional ion-transport channels, as illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202305190-fig-0006">6e</a>. Specifically, 1) 0D CoPS QDs were packaged into carbon “leaves”, which can afford robust buffer layer to relieve the mechanical stress caused by volume evolution upon Na<sup>+</sup> de-intercalation, presenting the stable cyclic lifespan; 2) More remarkable conductivity and higher Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption of the CoPS than individual CoS and CoP<sub>2</sub> can further facilitate faster Na<sup>+</sup>-transport and charge-transfer, rendering the superior rate performance and high capacitive behavior; 3) All 2D carbon “leaves” grown on 1D conductive N-CNF “branches” to produce a second-level conductive configuration, which accelerate the long-distance&nbsp;electronic transmission and guarantee the fast de-/sodiation capabilities of the electrode, besides, carbon “leaves” packaged CoPS QDs can adequately expose rich active sites, endowing the attractive specific capacity of the CoPS@C@N-CNF; 4) 1D&nbsp;N-CNF neural network can offer isotropous ion-transport channels along with the 1D radial direction, thereby rendering the sufficient electron and electrolyte supply for the carbon “leaves”; 5) More importantly, a&nbsp;mass&nbsp;of&nbsp;the second-level conductive structure composing of 2D carbon “leaves” modified 1D N-CNF “branches” are intertwined with each other, constructing a superior conductive 3D neural network, which can induce anisotropic ion-transport channels along with the intricate 3D network, ensuring the fast Na<sup>+</sup> kinetics at high rates.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202305190-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202305190-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, CoPS QDs were successfully introduced into a leaf-shape MOFs-derived conductive carbon matrix, which was further in situ grown on 3D branch-like N-CNF, forming a finely hierarchical leaf-branch-shaped CoPS@C@N-CNF configuration. Applied for SIBs anode for the first time, 3D branch-leaf-shaped CoPS@C@N-CNF exerts great superiorities for high-efficiency sodium storage including superior structural stability, enhanced electronic conductivity, fast ion-transport, rich reaction active-sites, and small volume change, thereby achieving outstanding reversible capacity and cyclic lifespan of 10&nbsp;000 cycles with a capacity of 126.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 20.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, as well as good rate performance. A full cell was assembled and exhibited great proof-of-feasibility for practical applications in terms of its fully stable cyclic endurance of 1000 cycles at 3.0&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and superior rate capability. In situ XRD combined with ex situ TEM and SAED results affords the forceful evidence for phase evolution mechanism from CoPS to Na<sub>2</sub>S, Na<sub>3</sub>P, and Co during initial cycling. Additionally. Na<sup>+</sup>-adsorption ability and Na<sup>+</sup>-diffusion kinetics properties were explored with the aid of DFT calculations in detail, demonstrating a higher Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption energy and lower diffusion energy barrier of CoPS compared to individual CoS and CoP<sub>2</sub>. This work not only endows a unique perspective in the innovative construction of 3D hierarchical ternary MPS<i><sub>x</sub></i>-based architecture in SIBs, but also resolves the volume expansion/ sluggish kinetics, and inferior cyclic lifespan of MPS<i><sub>x</sub></i> that often exist in SIB systems.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">

                  <li data-bib-id="adma202305190-bib-0002"><span class="bullet">2</span><span class="author">Z. Xiong</span>, <span class="author">H. Shi</span>, <span class="author">W.
